Free Talk

A Laughing Matter 188

—Seafarer

Father—Lately my health is declining. So I plan to gradually wind down all my affairs. Last week, I already made my will. All my assets after my death will be entirely inherited by you.

Son—Then what are you waiting for?

▲Manager (to a job applicant)—Are you married?

Applicant—Yes, I am.

Manager—Do you have children?

Applicant—I have six children in total. That's why I must have a job.

Manager—How long have you been married?

Applicant—Only a month and a half.

Manager—Nonsense! Married for a month and a half. How can you have six children?

Applicant—Because I married a widow. She brought six "oil bottles" [children] along.

Mother—Child, you should be generous. Let your little brother play with the stone bullet for a while. He will return it to you later.

Son—He'll take it and swallow it, and won't return it to me.

Mother—That can't be! He'll definitely return it to you.

Son—Because I saw him swallow two of them into his stomach.

▲A—Is your fiancée beautiful?

B—How could she not be? As soon as she gets on the tram, all the male passengers stop looking at the advertisements above the windows.

In Memory of Aviator Li Fengxuan 189

— Huang Jiping

Years ago, when I was a guest in Xiamen, Fujian, I knew two famous aviators: one was Mr. Chen Wenlin, and the other was Mr. Li Fengxuan. Chen stayed in Germany for many years. Last spring, he flew the "Xiamen" aircraft from Europe back to China, covering over 50,000 miles, setting the first long-distance flight record for a Chinese pilot. The naval authorities subsequently appointed him to the important position of director of the Xiamen Aviation Office. Li studied in the United States in his early years, mastering the art of flying. Upon returning to China, he served as an aviator in Guangdong Province. In 1926, he joined the Northern Expedition and made many outstanding contributions. When the "May 30th Incident" occurred, overseas Fujianese in the Philippines were angered by the rampant behavior of the Japanese and sought ways to serve their country and save their people. They initiated an aviation school in Xiamen to train talents for the nation, and they hired Mr. Li as an instructor. Both Chen and Li were from Xiamen, and they served their hometown together. Thus, almost all Fujianese knew of these two outstanding figures. The two gentlemen were childhood friends, and we became good friends at first sight, regretting that we had not met sooner. During our leisure time, we often went on excursions together, sharing our innermost thoughts and discussing the past and present. Our friendship was unmatched.

Last winter, I left Xiamen to return to my hometown. When bidding farewell, Chen held my hand and said, "I will be traveling to Fujian tomorrow. You are leaving a day earlier than me. I must write a song of farewell, otherwise, we will surely miss each other." Unfortunately, Brother Fengxuan had affairs in Zhangzhou and Longyan, soaring through the sky and working hard to suppress the communists. Knowing of your journey, he asked me to convey a word to express his regret at our parting. I said, "This gentleman is truly sentimental." We laughed together and parted. This spring, I had business in Shanghai, and my southern tour was canceled. Although we could no longer have the same joyful gatherings as before, exchanging letters was enough to ease my feelings. Last month, Li sent me a letter from Guangdong, detailing the merger of the Xiamen school into the Guangdong Aviation School this autumn and his promotion to chief instructor. He said that he trained students daily, soaring through the clouds, and his enthusiasm was greater than ever. He also said that the military order had been issued, and he would soon set sail to conquer Guangxi and eliminate the rebels. He would provide a detailed report after his triumphant return. His lingering feelings overflowed between the lines. I was celebrating this gentleman's talent and youth, when tragic news arrived. Mr. Li encountered an accident on the morning of the 4th of this month on the Dasha River in Guangzhou. At first, I did not believe it, but after receiving a quick letter from a friend in Guangdong detailing the incident, I confirmed it through news reports and finally understood. Alas, this man suffered such a fate. It can be said that an extraordinary person suffered an extraordinary disaster. How tragic was this?

According to the letter, the accident was due to a mechanical failure, not a lack of skill. The aircraft he was flying was the "Asia-Africa-England" No. 6, which was transferred from the Xiamen school to the Guangdong school. Mr. Li usually flew this aircraft and was extremely familiar with its operation. Who knew that when flying at an altitude of 2,000 feet, the engine suddenly broke down, and the tail cable also snapped simultaneously, causing it to be impossible to propel forward, rotating and falling down. Thus, the tragic accident happened. Is Mr. Li's death destined by fate? According to the post-mortem examination, Mr. Li and his companion, Liu Quan, were tightly fastened to the aircraft with leather belts. Therefore, when the aircraft sank to the bottom of the sea, it was difficult to escape. If they had not been wearing these belts at the beginning of the accident, they would have been able to float and survive. Perhaps Mr. Li did not pay attention to it in the panic. What is even more painful is that the aircraft could not be retrieved immediately after it sank. Four fishing boats were hired to cooperate with military electric boats to use nets to salvage it. It took two hours to lift the aircraft. The mechanical parts were not greatly damaged, but the bodies had turned color and swelled, with blood flowing from the facial features. The sight was unbearable to witness.

Mr. Li was upright in nature, resolute in his actions, and did not decline from hard work or complaints. He was a rare find among his peers, only thirty-five years old.

A Record of the Third Municipal Elementary School Sports Meet 190

— Ms. Ye Hua

Recently, the largest meeting in the country was the Fourth Plenary Session, and the largest meeting in Shanghai was the Third Joint Sports Meet of Municipal Elementary Schools. One is a major national event, and the other is a major event for elementary school students. Both events opened on the anniversary of the birth of Sun Yat-sen, which can be said to be a distant counterpart. In terms of the number of participants and the grandeur of the situation, the latter actually surpassed the former. However, the nature is different. The Municipal Elementary School Sports Meet is held annually, and the reporter is fortunate enough to participate each time. How fortunate it is. The anecdotes of previous sessions have been recorded in this column. Now, I will continue to present them on the left.

▲Comparison of Past and Present: The joint sports meet of Shanghai municipal elementary schools began in the autumn of 1928, when Wei Pengdan was the director of the bureau and Wang Zulan was the director of the second department. The president of the conference was the director of the bureau. The second session continued to do so. However, the director of the bureau has been replaced by Chen Daiqiu, and the director of the department is Ni Wenya. The leader of Shanghai education changes every year. When he delivered the opening speech, it was full of emotion. The cost of the conference was 1,000 yuan for the first session, 900 yuan for the second session, and 700 yuan for this session. Efficiency and funding are not directly proportional. 64 schools joined in the first year, 62 last year, and this year there are 61 municipal schools and 23 private schools. The most spectacular assembly exercise had 3,714 participants in the first session, 4,445 in the second session, and 4,516 in this session. The audience was twice as large as before, exceeding 20,000 each day. The Two Jiangs Women's Physical Education School suspended classes for three days to attend the conference, which shows its grand scale.

▲A Glimpse of the Venue: The rostrum faces south as before, with no changes compared to the past. The characters "Sports Meet" are hung in the middle of the plaque. Next to it is a couplet that says, "Boost your spirits and see who achieves true athletic success in these three days. Continue to train and strive to become healthy and strong citizens of China in ten years." The track is to the north. Each school's seats are arranged in advance, like pigeonholes, surrounding the four sides of the venue. The hawkers shouting at the top of their lungs are clustered in the gaps. Although the seats have been arranged, cuckoo nesting on magpie nests has been observed in reality. The importance of order and discipline in sports seems to have been forgotten. The rest areas are separated for men and women, and the children resting there are no different from a refugee map. The enthusiasm of these children cannot be matched by adults. Thinking of Bai Juyi's poem, "At twenty, one begins to grow up. At thirty, one begins to age. The color of peach and plum in the mirror cannot last for ten years," I feel even more emotional.

▲Square Table Takes Revenge for Round Chair: Before the assembly exercise, the students stand in a row, singing the Party song and the sports meet song. Zhong Zitong is invited to conduct. Mr. Zhong stands on a platform made up of three tables, singing and gesturing energetically. After the song, he is pleased with himself. He jumps from the platform to the table, and the round chair is crushed because he is too fat. The audience is filled with surprise and joy in the tense atmosphere. When Wang Huaiqi takes the stage again to perform a model exercise, one of the legs of the highest square table suddenly tilts, threatening to collapse. The situation is serious. The staff rushes forward to hold the four legs of the table, which is comical. People say it is a new-style human pyramid. The reporter says that the round chair was innocently trampled on, and the square table is taking revenge for it.

▲Sports Meet and Bathing: In recent years, the Songjiang Girls' High School has won the most awards in the women's division of the Jiangsu Provincial High School Sports Meet. The school's athletes, Fu Xuezhen and Lü Tianzhi, are now teaching at a certain municipal school this summer. They led the athletes, Zhu Songju and Qian Yunlan, to participate in the event, predicting that their results would be good. After all, strong generals have no weak soldiers under their command. However, the two were disheartened and said to the reporter, "China has been running new education for more than 30 years, and sports meets have also been held for more than 30 years. There are tens of millions of sports meets of all sizes across the country. However, Chinese people are still stooping and hunching, and their faces are still pale. It is still impossible to develop the habit of bathing once a day, like in England, America, and Germany. What about sports meets? What about sports meets?"

New Chrysanthemum Poetry 191

— Wang Wenru

Why is it called "new"? Today's chrysanthemums are different from the chrysanthemums of the past. Today's people's attitude towards chrysanthemums is also different from that of the people of the past. That is, the flower is an expression of the person. Readers of my poems will not be far from understanding.

Adopting elegance and criticizing at will, vulgar people diligently examine the classics. Don't say that culture is truly swept away, they can still pick out flower themes. (There are still many types of chrysanthemums today. Vulgar people, showing off their culture, often add comments. The text is not related to the topic, which is ridiculous. My friend, Mr. Pan Gongzhan, also has a commentary sentence, which is quite elegant in its wording. If benevolence is superior, then learning may be the case.)

Born to be parasitic on fences, purple, white, yellow, and red each express their strangeness. Occupying the ninth autumn, they boast of their appearance. Laughing at when will their old age be. (What was once called cold fragrance and secluded beauty has now changed its original appearance. Try to question it with the sentence "Lonely, proud of the world, with whom to hide" in the Red Chamber. The chrysanthemum has no words to answer. Alas, things are like this, how can people bear it?)

Disgusted to enter the hermit's home back then, lamenting the warmth and coldness of the world in general. Hot officials and wealthy merchants arrange banquets for appreciation. This is also a rich and noble flower in the human world.

Grand gatherings are opened, displaying ten thousand pots. The city government calls for them, surpassing mountain villages. Don't say that the price of yellow flowers is cheap, a single look can win one yuan. (Shanghai's Nanjing Road is holding a chrysanthemum exhibition to collect famous varieties for viewing. The ticket price is one yuan. Recalling that when foreigners established this meeting a few years ago, the example was three yuan. Now it has been reduced by more than half.)

Silently harboring hatred, it is pitiful to be born. No wonder heaven indulges in worldly sentiments. Purity is specially taught to reside in muddy places. Knitting their brows and complaining bitterly to Tao Yuanming. (The beautiful scenery of the Eastern Fence has also changed, appreciating the praise of hot officials and wealthy merchants. If Tao Yuanming were still alive, he would also have to give up his love.)

Peaceful times in the Eastern Sea have many new images, while a bleak Western River reveals cracks. Asking the surviving elders, can the pine and chrysanthemum of Sang Sang still exist?

Discussing where to build a thatched hut, walking is too unbearable in the thorns. I have no share in picking the dew and flowers. It is difficult to find Chrysanthemum Pond to avoid Qin.

Who planted miscellaneous species at the door, countless autumn appearances, long for children and grandchildren. Intermingled colors openly surpass the correct color, startling to see the yellow race lost its soul.

Travel Notes from Southeast Asia (74) 192

— Ling Hua

The car moved southwest very slowly, stopping frequently. There were hardly any villages, all on mountain peaks, rising above the ground at an altitude of 1,700 to 1,800 feet. Looking down, the mountains were all below the car, an endless green sea. Half bamboo, half trees. If a paper mill could be built, I wonder if it would be suitable. The poem says:

The railway car travels south, mountains filled with bamboo forests. An endless green sea swayed, listening to the chirping birds at will.

Few thatched huts and wild people, tangled vines and dense trees. Knowing that it is a secluded place, the waterfall roars like a dragon's song.

These natural forests have no owners, all taken over by the government, so their benefits are endless. On the way, I occasionally saw men and women planting things on the mountain tops, carrying knives. In this place, one cannot defend against snakes and beasts without carrying a knife. At seven o'clock, we arrived at Namtu. Red and white Western-style houses, lit by electric lights. The mountain slopes were all flat. The mountains of northern Burma have no steep cliffs, so they are most suitable for planting. Not like the high and steep mountains of Hong Kong, which are harsh on people. Namtu is vast and wide, completely within the scope of a silver company. Only the rich have their own cars. There are no other cars to be found. Luggage is carried by porters. Initially, I thought that the Burmese in Yangon did not know how to carry things on poles, and I had not seen anyone wearing a hat. In northern Burma, they wear hats and there are many carriers. Their hats are made of large bamboo skin, beautiful and strong. Passing a large bridge, the water flowed very quickly. I stayed at the residence of Liang Jinshan, who is the famous "Old Man Liang," from Yongchang, who commanded more than 2,000 workers, contracted railway projects, and earned 100,000 to 200,000 at a time, becoming rich. He is generous, and highly respected in the labor community.

Zhang Dexi enthusiastically told me that six or seven stations from Namtu, and four or five stations from Lashio, in the northeast, there is the land of the Five Kalias, residing between the English and the Chinese. The area is a thousand miles, rich in silver mines, and also has gold. Wu Sangui once operated it in ancient times. Recently, the British and Americans have been coveting it. According to the mining engineer, its silver is ten times that of Namtu. The British once went to mine it, but were rejected by the Kalia people. When Chinese go to mine it, the Kalia people kill cows to welcome them. Many of its people are Muslims. It is now possible to find ways to exploit it. I agreed very much. Zhang's father made a map of all of Burma, detailing the products, especially the five metals and precious jade produced in northern Burma.

European Travel Correspondence (86) 193

— Liu Haisu

▲Pilgrimage to Italy Diary

(3) Ten Days in Rome (9)

Day Two—Colosseum—Arch of Constantine—Baths of Caracalla—Catacombs

When the Roman sun shone brightly, we left the Baths of Caracalla together, boarded a carriage, whipped the horses forward, and followed a winding path, leaning against the Esquiline Hill, turning into a grove of green trees, and then ascended a steep slope, which seemed to be a hill, neatly lined with delicate cypresses.

"Catacombs!" the carriage driver shouted loudly behind us. We hurriedly got off the carriage and stepped on the traces of the year 100 AD, the so-called underground chapel of the "Catacombs."

Entering the Church of Saint Sebastian, we saw the former tomb of Saint Sebastian, with a white stone statue of Saint Sebastian lying there. He seemed to be looking back at us, wondering how these few Chinese youths, who do not follow religion, could come from afar to pay homage. We walked back and forth in the solemn and gloomy church, circling a few times. We saw several stone carvings of the life of the Virgin, filled with clusters of lilies on the altar and in the shrine. The only impression was a clean and mysterious one: clean. It was truly a pure land, nothing else. I really couldn't imagine that prosperous Europe would also have this quiet and extinct phenomenon. In this lonely hall, only one devout pilgrim was kneeling before the ruined altar, murmuring. We stood still, lingering, somewhat hesitant. Just as a young monk came out of the room next to the tomb of Saint Sebastian, we stepped forward, bowed our hands, and asked:—

"Are the underground chapel and the underground tomb here?"

He replied, "This is it."

So he led us into the warehouse-like, dark gray door and gave each of us a white candle like a penholder, had us light it, and then, holding the key, we entered the catacombs and went into the so-called underground chapel of the Catacombs.

"This is where Saint Sebastian preached on that day. This is his statue."

The monk who led us held the dim candlelight in his right hand and pointed up and down with his left finger as he spoke.

The monk told us many legends of Saint Sebastian, the stories of all the believers being greatly suppressed and persecuted, and some myths.

Special Edition for the Canadian Trade Delegation

Canadian Trade Delegation Arrives in Shanghai 194

Arrived in port at eleven o'clock yesterday morning; the municipal government hosted a banquet in the evening.

Visiting factories today, departing for Hong Kong tomorrow.

A Word of Respect to the Canadian Trade Delegation (Pan Gongzhan) 195

Canada and our Republic of China, located on the east and west sides of the Pacific Ocean, are both vast and rich in resources, and should be able to cooperate and benefit from trade. Therefore, when this Canadian Trade Delegation set out on its eastern tour last month, our government and business community immediately prepared to receive them sincerely. Now that all the members of the delegation arrived in Shanghai yesterday (16th), we should naturally express our warm welcome to strengthen the friendship between the two countries.

However, we also want to take this opportunity to express our hopes to Canadian business leaders. Trade between the two countries benefits both parties, but must be built on a foundation of equal treatment and goodwill. Last year, Canadian goods shipped to China reached US$23.5 million, while Chinese goods shipped to Canada were only worth US$3 million. Compared between the two countries, China had a trade deficit of over US$20 million. Its benefits to Canada are conceivable. This is because China's industries are not prosperous and its products are not abundant, so it can only feel ashamed. However, the Canadian government's suppression of Chinese goods and harsh treatment of Chinese immigrants are also factors. Leaving aside other matters, the Canadian government's ban on Asian immigration is already considered very unfair. In East Asia, China and Japan are of course both major powers. The Canadian government has negotiated a secret agreement with Japan, allowing 150 Japanese immigrants to enter each year, while strictly rejecting Chinese people. The harsh Article 43 of 1923 was specifically designed to oppress Chinese immigrants. Even the wives and children of Chinese immigrants are not allowed to enter Canada. Chinese immigrants returning to China must have a limited period. Import inspections are extremely harsh, and after entering the country, they are often suppressed by local governments. Despite their vows to fight to the death, Chinese immigrants have had no success. Our National Government and the business community are all familiar with these issues. Under such unequal treatment, seeking a balanced and mutually beneficial development of trade between the two countries is like climbing a tree to catch fish. Since the Canadian business leaders have come to China with the purpose of expanding trade in East Asia, they should first investigate the facts that hinder goodwill between China and Canada, and try to remove these obstacles, so that the practical benefits of trade can be achieved.

What the people of our Republic of China need is not that Chinese merchants or overseas Chinese have any special privileges in Canada, but only that overseas Chinese and other foreign people traveling in Canada, and Chinese goods and other foreign goods shipped to Canada, enjoy equal treatment. We deeply hope that the members of the Canadian Trade Delegation will make efforts in this regard after returning home from their tour of the East.

Situation of the Delegation's Arrival in Shanghai 196

▲ This trip is of a preparatory nature ▲ The official inspection delegation will come to China next year.

The Canadian Far East Trade Delegation arrived at the New Customs Wharf at 11:00 AM yesterday aboard the Empress of Japan. Representatives of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Chen Shiguang and Liu Yunfang, representatives of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, Shou Jingwei, and representatives of the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau welcomed the delegation at the wharf. After arriving in Shanghai, the delegation stayed at the Cathay Hotel on the Bund in Nanjing Road. The head of the delegation, Mr. Emery, and the secretary of the delegation, Mr. Clarke, met with our reporter yesterday and stated that the delegation inspected Japan for two weeks. This time, they came to China because they needed to rush back to their country to celebrate Christmas. Therefore, the time was very short. Moreover, this trip to China was of a preparatory nature, hoping to contact leading figures in Chinese politics and business in advance in preparation for sending an official inspection delegation to China next year to conduct a long-term study of trade conditions between the two countries. However, it is a great pity that this time they cannot stay in China for a few more days. It is now scheduled to leave Shanghai on Tuesday for Hong Kong, and then to Guangzhou, staying in Sanbu for a total of two weeks. There is no time to visit Nanjing and the North. This is our first time in Shanghai, and we feel that Shanghai is a very developed city, worthy of being the center of China's economy, finance, industry, and commerce. Shanghai's imports account for half of the country's total. Canada is also paying close attention to the Greater Shanghai Plan, which will make it a beautiful city and a center of culture and education. Shanghai goods were imported into Canada beginning in 1869, and Canadian goods were shipped to Shanghai beginning in 1871. Half of the people on the Pacific coast of Canada are of Chinese descent.

Members of the Canadian Trade Delegation 197

The members of the Canadian Far East Trade Mission are mostly leaders from the country's industrial and commercial sectors. For example, the head of the delegation, John M. Imrie, is the manager of the Edmonton Journal, Canadian Newspaper, and Sassoon Printing Bureau. The other members are either financial tycoons or industrial experts. Their respective professions are listed as follows:

Department Store Industry: J. Edmond Lebreoque

Industrial and Commercial Expert: Max Steinkoff

Last Night, the City Government Hosted a Banquet for the Entire Delegation 198

▲Secretary-General Yu delivered a welcome speech on behalf of the Mayor—Hoping that, in addition to investigating business, they will maintain peace between the two countries.

At 8 o'clock last night, the Shanghai Municipal Government hosted a banquet at the Xing Hua Lou Restaurant for the Canadian Trade Mission. Attending were all members of the delegation, Secretary-General Yu Hongjun of the Municipal Government and his wife, bureau chiefs, Chen Shiguang, representative of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Zhao Jinqing, representative of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and Shou Yicheng, as well as the U.S. Commercial Counselor, among others. Secretary-General Yu Hongjun delivered a welcome speech on behalf of the Mayor, first expressing his welcome, and then stating that although the Canadian trade mission came to Shanghai to investigate business, they should also bear the mission of maintaining peace between the two countries, treat overseas Chinese in Canada on an equal footing, and strive for mutual benefit in all aspects, etc. Subsequently, Chen Shiguang rose to speak, hoping for peace between the two countries and wishing the delegation members good health. Finally, delegation leader John M. Imrie gave a reply. The event concluded at 11 o'clock.

▲Reply from Delegation Leader John M. Imrie 199

Delegation leader John M. Imrie gave a reply, saying, "I am deeply grateful for the hospitality extended to us this evening. I am honored to be the Vice-President of the Canadian Chamber of Commerce. The Chamber of Commerce represents the chambers of commerce of 205 cities in Canada. I extend, on their behalf, congratulations to the Chinese government and people. Canada is only now beginning to understand the significance of China's political changes. In the past, we were confused by the various developments in China's politics and military due to a lack of understanding. Fortunately, we are now gradually understanding that these changes are not just phenomena of conflict and division, but rather precursors to major reforms and progress. China's achievements in recent decades could not be achieved in other countries in hundreds of years. China's current reforms, such as in education, society, politics, and industry, have taken our ancestors four centuries to achieve, while China has made astonishing progress in less than thirty years. This is largely due to China's experience, philosophy, and civilization of over five thousand years. This rich heritage has greatly contributed to its modern transformation. Compared to the long history of Chinese culture, the last thirty or fifty years are like a fleeting moment. This temporary transition will soon be forgotten and submerged in the greater political, economic, industrial, and social life of the future. We in Canada deeply appreciate China's historical civilization and philosophical contributions to the world. McGill University in Montreal, one of the most famous universities, has established a special department to study it. Mutual understanding between China and Canada is beneficial to both. The current Canadian trade mission has close ties to commercial and economic matters. Through personal contact, we can advance international understanding and goodwill, especially among the countries bordering the Pacific Ocean. Changes in economics and transportation are creating a new international community along the Pacific Ocean, and the center of world commerce is gradually shifting from the Atlantic to the Pacific. Old commercial practices are gradually being eliminated, and new commercial relationships are being established. This will affect not only one or two continents, but the entire world's commerce is in a vortex. Resources such as people, raw materials, sea routes, human needs, intelligence, and talent will inevitably concentrate in the Pacific, and China will play an important role in this Pacific international community because of its vast land, abundant resources, large population, long historical experience, and long-standing philosophical traditions. When China passes through its current period of transition, and its politics, finance, and commerce enter a period of stability, its transportation, trade, and commerce will greatly develop, becoming one of the world's great industrial and economic powers. It will join hands with its Pacific friends like brotherly nations to strive for a better position. Although Canada has a short history, it can also play an important role among its friendly nations because it came into contact with other countries on the Pacific relatively late and therefore has more suitable elements. Canada stretches four thousand miles from east to west. It has only been one hundred and forty years since white people traversed this continent and first discovered the direct access to the Pacific coast, and even sixty years ago, the population of western Canada was still less than one hundred thousand. Therefore, among the Pacific friendly nations, Canada has a simpler history and has never had misunderstandings or animosity with other countries, nor has it ever caused conflict or war. Canada has no political or economic ambitions towards its friendly nations other than maintaining peace and promoting mutually beneficial trade. Therefore, it is better suited to assist its older friends on the Pacific coast to jointly maintain peace in the Pacific and to seek ways to enhance it. Moreover, the Pacific friendly nations cannot form a closed community that does not engage in beneficial exchanges with the outside world. With today's rapid transportation and close trade relations, a world where remote places are like neighbors and the world is one family has been created. Canada can also make unique contributions to this larger scope of world peace because Canada is located in the middle of the Far East and the United Kingdom. It has had two hundred and fifty years of political and commercial relations with its mother country, and with China, the first voyage of the Canadian Shipping Company's ships across the Pacific was in 1888. Since then, the commercial exchanges and personal contacts between the two sides have become increasingly frequent. Therefore, Canada, contacting the United Kingdom across the Atlantic and China across the Pacific, has been doing so for many years. Can it not serve as a mediator between these two great countries, conveying the actual situation of one country to the other, in order to help maintain and promote understanding and goodwill between the two countries? Canada and the United States of America share a three-thousand-mile border. For over a hundred years, they have taken it upon themselves to convey the actual situation to each other between the United States and the United Kingdom. Can they not now take the position of conveying the truth between America and Asia? Moreover, Canada has a latent force in maintaining world peace. The people of Canada are based on the English and French ethnic groups. At the beginning of colonization, the people of the two countries lived separately. By 1760, Canada was entirely under British rule. The struggle between the two ethnic groups for leadership had been decided. Since then, they have been cooperating sincerely, trusting and working together, and both have contributed to the creation of a new national character. Therefore, Canada is not only adjacent to the Pacific friendly nations because it is located on the Pacific coast, and is politically linked to the United Kingdom, and is linked to the United States by close ties, but its ethnicity is also linked to the Latin ethnic groups of Europe."

Appeal from Overseas Chinese in Canada 202

—Telegram from Wu Ruoquan and others to representatives of the Shanghai Party, Government, Military, and Business Sectors—

▲Demanding Equal Treatment▲Appealing for National Assistance

Overseas Chinese in Canada, Wu Ruoquan and others, sent an express telegram saying: "To the Shanghai Municipal Party Committee, Director Chen of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Office in Shanghai, Mayor Zhang of Shanghai, and the directors of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce: The British Canadian Chamber of Commerce has initiated the organization of a Far East trade mission, which set off for China last month and will arrive in Shanghai in the coming days. However, our compatriots overseas have suffered from various harsh regulations imposed by their government in recent years, and their livelihoods are on the verge of collapse. Now that the trade mission is coming to China, we have heard that our authorities and business leaders are preparing to welcome them, but there is no avenue for the appeals of overseas Chinese in Canada. We should find ways to help them and save them. Wu Ruoquan and others have resided in Canada for many years and have witnessed the Canadian government's mistreatment of our overseas Chinese compatriots and its trade with China. The situation is extremely tragic. We will now present the facts as follows:

According to the Canadian government's 1929 trade report with China, Canadian goods imported into China were worth 27,007,997 yuan in national currency, while Chinese goods exported and sold in Canada were worth 4,497,796 yuan in national currency. This means that our country lost 22,510,201 yuan in national currency in trade with Canada in one year. In addition, with the losses from freight charges for Canadian ships carrying goods and passengers, the total loss to Canada in one year should be over 30 million yuan. How can we reverse this loss of over 30 million yuan each year? This is a major issue that urgently needs to be studied and addressed today. Imposing tariff policies and restricting the import of Canadian industrial products to protect the development of our domestic industries are all matters that our government should pay attention to. For example, our country's tea and silk are traditionally major export commodities, but there is a trend in Canada of using Japanese silk to replace Chinese silk and Indian tea to replace Chinese tea. Our country should improve its silk products to compete with Japan and improve its tea products to compete with India, so that Canadians will welcome our country's tea and silk, in order to increase the quantity of our tea and silk sold in Canada and thereby reverse the losses in trade with Canada. We should also imitate the example of Canadian merchants coming to China to conduct investigations and organize overseas trade missions to Canada to investigate their needs, with the aim of transporting various products other than tea and silk to Canada for sale. These are all matters that our merchants should pay attention to. The above are the key tasks that Wu Ruoquan and others sincerely hope that our government and business leaders will strive to develop in trade with Canada.

Alas, do the Canadians say that overseas Chinese are taking away their jobs and lowering their standard of living? Not only is Canada vast and sparsely populated, but it also needs to increase its population to develop its industries. In terms of reason, this does not match the facts. Is it that the Canadian government is only welcoming European immigrants? Recently, hundreds of thousands of European immigrants have entered Canada each year. How can they explain their welcoming one group while rejecting another? The reason why Canadians are discriminating against our overseas Chinese is not only an economic issue, but is also driven by racial prejudice. Can our government and our people bear to sit idly by as our overseas Chinese are heavily oppressed by the government and people of their place of residence without lending a helping hand? Can they accept the humiliation of foreigners treating us as an inferior race without thinking of ways to wash away this shame? The late Dr. Sun Yat-sen said that overseas Chinese are the mother of the revolution. Many of our overseas Chinese have devoted themselves to the improvement of domestic politics, economy, society, and education. Now, our overseas Chinese are in a struggle for survival, and they hope that our government and people will work together to alleviate their suffering, just as people in a severe drought hope for rain clouds. Now that the Canadian trade mission is coming to the East, it is a good opportunity for our government and people to lend a helping hand. We humbly request that government authorities and business leaders, when discussing matters with Canadian merchants, either warn them or explain the advantages and disadvantages, so that after they return to their country, they can include this in their report and urge their government to become aware and amend or cancel the various harsh regulations mentioned above, especially the amendment to the 1924 Immigration Act, which is the urgent need of overseas Chinese. For example, the requirement that overseas Chinese must return to Canada within two years of leaving should be changed to five years. Also, the requirement that merchants entering the country must have a capital of 2,500 gold yuan and are limited to engaging in import and export business should be changed to not adding any restrictions on the type of business they can engage in. Also, the restrictions on merchants' children entering the country should be removed. Also, the restriction that students must leave Canada immediately after graduation should be changed to allowing them to reside freely in Canada for practical experience. Moreover, there has been talk of establishing a Sino-Canadian commercial treaty in recent years. We especially hope that our diplomatic authorities will, at that time, adhere to the principles of equality and mutual benefit and stipulate clauses that allow overseas Chinese in Canada to enjoy the same treatment as overseas Chinese from other countries, in order to improve the situation of overseas Chinese. This is for the sake of the overseas Chinese themselves and for the sake of the national economy. This is what we overseas Chinese sincerely hope that our government and business leaders will do. The overseas Chinese are suffering and are in dire need of help. If our government authorities and business compatriots rise up to save them, not only will the overseas Chinese be grateful, but it will also be the good fortune of the nation. Overseas Chinese in Canada: Wu Ruoquan, Zeng Yangfu, Cheng Tianfang, Lai Lian, Huang Huabiao, Zhao Weiping, Li Mianchen, Guan Suren, Huang Zhongwen, Situ Langchuan, November 10, 1930.

Furthermore, since our country is an economically backward country, the deficit in our foreign trade relies on the wages and small profits earned by overseas Chinese residing in those countries to offset it. It is estimated that there are over 40,000 overseas Chinese residing in Canada. Assuming that each person, on average, earns 200 yuan in national currency each year after deducting expenses in Canada, the total amount remitted back to China would be over 8 million yuan in national currency. This amount is sufficient to compensate for part of the losses in trade with Canada. Our overseas Chinese drift to foreign lands for the sake of earning a living for themselves and for the sake of compensating for trade losses for the country. However, they suffer from the oppression of local governments and the rejection of the people. Their plight is unspeakable. We respectfully present this to our government authorities and business leaders in detail.

In recent years, anti-Chinese sentiment has permeated throughout Canada. The reasons they hold are: saving domestic workers from unemployment, maintaining high wage levels, maintaining a high standard of living, and saying that inferior Chinese cannot assimilate with them. They fabricate these inappropriate reasons and develop various harsh regulations to oppress our overseas Chinese.

(1) To Restrict Overseas Chinese from Entering the Country 203

In 1924, the Canadian government revised the Immigration Act, stipulating that all Chinese laborers are not allowed to enter the country. Merchants must have a capital of over 2,500 Canadian dollars and be solely engaged in import and export business before they are allowed to enter the country. These merchants can only enter the country alone and cannot bring their wives and daughters. Students must have the qualifications to enter university and must leave the country immediately after graduation and are not allowed to reside there. Moreover, when the Immigration Bureau implements this regulation, it interrogates those entering the country from the business and academic circles in various ways, making things difficult. If they are suspected of anything, they are rejected. Therefore, it is extremely difficult for those newly going to Canada to enter the country. The Immigration Department also registers those residing in Canada. A considerable number of people have been rejected and deported because their registration procedures are not complete. From now on, our overseas Chinese will disappear from Canada.

(2) To Exclude Chinese Laborers from Factories 204

Factories employ Chinese laborers because they are hardworking and can work for long hours with extremely low wages. It is said that their treatment is already far different from that of Canadian workers. However, after the Canadian government promulgated the maximum working hours regulation, it also promulgated the minimum wage regulation. As a result, overseas Chinese have been excluded from factories one after another. Even those who remain have been forced by labor unions to dismiss them. Overseas Chinese have fallen into the misery of unemployment.

(3) To Prohibit Chinese Businesses from Employing White Women 205

Overseas Chinese in central Canada mostly run restaurants and employ white women as waitresses to attract customers and earn more profits. Canadian businessmen are very jealous of this. However, according to the principle of freedom of industry, they cannot prevent overseas Chinese from operating this business. The governments of the central provinces have therefore promulgated a regulation prohibiting Chinese restaurants from employing white women. They are restricting their business by this regulation. If this regulation is not removed, our small Chinese businessmen will not be able to survive.

(4) To Establish Separate Schools for Yellow and White Children 206

The government of British Columbia in western Canada considers the Chinese to be an inferior race and fears that Chinese children will hinder the progress of white children. Based on this reason, it has enacted regulations prohibiting Chinese children from attending white schools and establishing separate Chinese schools to accommodate Chinese children. This measure not only prevents our overseas Chinese children from receiving the same education as white children, but also insults our nation in its meaning.

The above four are only the major points. In addition, there are various harsh regulations such as agricultural restrictions and laundry restrictions, which are even more difficult to enumerate.

Book and Newspaper Introductions

Film Magazine Nationalism Film Movement Special Issue 207

— Gao Wei

Edited by Lu Mengshu

Published by Wenhua Art and Book Company

What is film? What is film art? And what is film art supposed to express? In backward China, how many decent answers have there been to these questions? What is the state of the so-called domestic film industry? What do Chinese film audiences demand? What kind of films are needed in this era? Everything we see only evokes endless sorrow and sighing. People in the film business focus solely on making money, but what about film publications that have a guiding responsibility? They focus solely on "praising." It is truly rare to find anyone who makes a real contribution to Chinese film and Chinese film art.

Film is the eighth art among emerging arts, a comprehensive art that comes after literature, drama, music, dance, painting, architecture, and sculpture. We can say that film is a new art formed by the extreme development of modern human intelligence, successfully integrating various arts. Its field of development is based on three essential elements: industrial, scientific, and artistic. Without any one of them, it cannot succeed. In modern times, in all countries, it has almost occupied a great potential force. The general task it bears in the transportation of thought and in the determination of conceptual forms is becoming more and more active. It exposes the inherent national spirit and national characteristics of a nation and also promotes them. The presentation of national colors is indeed unusually clear and strong. But in reality, the importance attached to film by the general public is due to factual conditions. The incredible ability to control human behavior is cultivated through the various qualities, functions, and advantages of film. Thus, in quantity and substance, the hearts and emotions of the audience are easily lifted and engaged in unconscious appreciation. Because the expression of film is closest to the lifestyle of human beings, it directly fills the empty hearts of human beings, awakening and inspiring strong will, and forgetting all unfortunate defects from the fatigue of life. In the appreciation of the screen, one feels a new and bright force. Therefore, the formation of the universality of film has its own unique qualities.

But what is the situation of film when it is introduced to China? Film has only a very short history in China, but it has already flowed into a morbid and dangerously deformed development. On the surface, the Chinese people are indeed interested in film, but in essence, they still cannot shake off the old habits of the Chinese. They only see some superficial things and grasp some vague impressions. The so-called evaluation of Chinese films has nothing to say except to undermine the dignity of the national character. We simply cannot admit that those films are sufficient to represent our film industry. At the same time, it seems that there is a need to start all over again.

However, the reason why Chinese films have declined to this point may not be unrelated to the backwardness of Chinese literature and art, which has led to film also flowing into an unconscious state, failing to grasp the correct central idea for development. This is undeniable. Therefore, the biggest problem with Chinese films can be said to be the lack of true leaders of film art. As a result, it has been occupied by a group of shallow and boring people. Now, our literary and art circles have finally undergone a sudden and drastic change, advocating a nationalist literary and art movement that establishes the entire people as the central ideology. This will inevitably have a huge impact and form a new opportunity for film. The nationalist movement in literature and art has been generally recognized, and the national consciousness in film is also generally needed. We are just about to use the special qualities and functions of film to bear the current national mission. Similarly, in order to save the crisis of Chinese films, all those who work hard in film and are dissatisfied with the current situation of the Chinese film industry should gather in this category and jointly devote themselves to the nationalist film movement in order to fully reach the brilliant realm of Chinese films. Recently, in our film industry, the atmosphere in this regard seems to have attracted people's attention. We sincerely embrace unlimited prospects for the start of a new opportunity for Chinese films.

It was the "Film Magazine" that first discovered this movement and took on the responsibility of advocating it. Everyone who pays a little attention to Chinese films knows the reputation of Lu Mengshu, the editor of "Film," in the film industry. Mr. Lu deeply understands the objective and general task of film art and the trend of modern film art. Therefore, he resolutely erected the banner of the nationalist film movement. On the one hand, he followed the establishment of nationalism in literature and art, and on the other hand, he created new life by breaking through the huge crisis in the Chinese film industry. Mr. Lu's vision is truly worthy of our admiration and gratitude. Under this circumstance, we have seen the exposure of the theory of nationalist films in the previous issues one, two and three of "Film." Especially the third issue is even more distinct. But Mr. Lu still has greater ambitions, so he published the "Nationalist Film Movement Special Issue" in the fourth issue of "Film," seeking to further actively promote the power of this movement. This is a very gratifying thing for our future film

Page 18

industry, and we cannot help but pray for it.

In "Our Words," we further recognize the attitude of this special issue:

…Although film is mistakenly regarded as one of the entertainment tools by shallow and boring people, its own artistic value and mission have not disappeared because of it. Its emergence was originally the same as literature and art, an artwork produced in the ideological form formed on the standpoint of the nation. For this reason, our colleagues also followed the nationalists in literature and art and made a national film movement, and published a special issue in this issue of this journal as the beginning of this movement...

We certainly dare not be complacent, and we dare not boast. We are both indignant at the boredom of those who make a living from film and feel the decline of literature and art.

In order to demand the improvement of the film industry, we also demand national self-determination. Therefore, we try our best to elaborate on the ideological center of film, and we strive to instill national consciousness in people.

We have raised the banner, we have shouted, we have moved forward, and we have done it. People, Chinese people, you are facing a great crisis. You must rise up and participate in our work.

What a bright and honest attitude!

In terms of content, most of the texts in this issue belong to theoretical construction. Originally, at the beginning of a movement, theory is indeed the most important. Based on the correct theoretical foundation, we can proceed step by step to promote it. Here, let's briefly talk about a few main articles.

Bao Luoduo's "China Needs Films with National Characteristics" fully explains the issue of national characteristics in film. The author believes that films in all countries have their own national characteristics expressed in them, because "the characteristics of each nation should be indicated one by one, and people in the world will not pay attention to them. For this reason, we have to come out to discuss our nationalism." As for what national characteristics Chinese films should express, the author tells us that "the national characteristics of China are in what place, which artists should search for. Successful works of art do not have the characteristics of each nation, especially modern works of art are like this," and there is also one thing, "the characteristics of each nation can be in the process of evolution from time to time, which means that we should be responsible for creating it."

Li Chunsen's "Construction of Nationalist Films" first explains the various special advantages and potential of film, and points out the permanent halls of the United States, England, Germany, France, Russia, Italy, and Japan, and proves that the power of film to dominate the audience in recent years is so great that it cannot be ignored. Second, it elaborates on the relationship between film and the nation, and the objective conditions of film in this era. In the current state of literature and art that establishes a national center of consciousness, it is urgent to incorporate nationalism into film, and "in order to further clearly establish national consciousness and hope for its full development, the construction of nationalist films is an important task today." Third, the author examines the qualities contained in foreign films, and judges them from a broad perspective, discovering their common points. On the one hand, there is a firm and clear national consciousness, and on the other hand, it expresses the characteristics of the nation to which it belongs, eliminates all ideas that hinder its own nation, and promotes the will of its own nation to develop upward, expressing all the struggling and tragic history of its own nation in the process of increasing its own glory. In order to make it clear, the author also said one by one the national characteristics expressed in the films of various countries. Secondly, the international nature of film is also worth noting. Generally, in the process of development, a nation must let people recognize the advantages of its own nation and occupy a position in international culture. Therefore, film has become a medium. However, in modern imperialist countries, they often like to describe the ugliness of different nations to intersperse and set off their own pride, and our Chinese nation is one of the unlucky ones. Fourth, looking back at our Chinese film industry, we found that it is full of decline. Not only is the past disappointing, but "in the current huge crisis, it is still in the ascendant. The film industry is still deeply infected with deep-rooted poison in the big drum, and does not know how to be self-conscious and self-help. They do not have the long-term vision to do realistic research, they do not have literary and artistic evaluation, so they are obviously close to being blind and standing, leaving the nation and humanity behind." Fifth, is the author's general conclusion, affirming that in the current era, only the nationalist film movement is the only way out for the Chinese film industry. As for the construction of the nationalist film base, it proposes several main outlines: 1. Organize a strong and large-scale film company. 2. Train actors. 3. Create scripts. 4. Organize a nationalist film magazine.

Works of Painter Pang Xunqin 208

Qiu Yuan's "Nationality of Film," according to the editor, Qiu Yuan originally planned to write four or five thousand words, but unfortunately he couldn't think because of eye disease, so he reluctantly wrote this article. In the future, he will definitely write another article, so let's wait. The main purpose of this short article is that the author believes that the national color shown in the film is not only a fragment of the national color, but also the entire national spirit and national consciousness. As for the opinions of the film industry, he said, "Wait, let's first form our national consciousness about film, and then work hard to create our national film."

The editor himself said in the opening of "Nationalism and Chinese Film," "Film, a new artwork, is the only way out for nationalism, because it can not only give people a glimpse of the characteristics of a nation in history and personality, but also give people a glimpse of the manifestation of a national spirit in the development of personality. For this reason, we also have such an urgent need for Chinese and German films." The author also sought out the various reasons why we Chinese need nationalist films from many aspects. The author's paragraph is truly thorough.

Film is the newest and most powerful in literature and art. We can no longer make it deformed. We must now make it truly bear its own mission. We must now make it realize its own inherent center of consciousness—the true spirit of nationalism.

This true spirit of nationalism is the Western culture expressed in Western color TVs, and the love problem that is specially proposed in Western films for everyone to make a true solution, just like the masculine beauty and feminine beauty that are specially elaborated in Western films. In short, we must continue to work with the nationalism we are advocating. Gentlemen, gentlemen who make a living from film, please get up, please get up urgently, abandon the previous wrong ways, and establish the current nationalist film.

Tang Songgao's "China Should Have China's Emerging Films" clarifies the relationship between film and nationalism from the perspective of lifestyle, and also has unique insights on society, and is indeed a text worthy of attention. The author finally hopes, "The emergence of this new Chinese small national consciousness film art is the spiritual liberation of the weak Chinese nation."

In addition, there is Gao Jianhua's "Expression of the American National Spirit," which explains it with the United States as the object. Luo Baigao's "Rogue Emperor and French Nationality" uses the film Rogue Emperor to explain the state of the French nationality. Other texts are left for readers to understand by themselves.

The paintings in this issue are also very powerful, and most of them focus on the aspect of healthy beauty, so that our nation, which is known as the sick man, can feel something.

Looking at this "Film" as a whole, the contribution to our film industry is indeed not shallow. Although the text in this issue seems to be too biased towards one aspect of exploration, this kind of theoretical construction also plants the impression of basic concepts in general. I sincerely hope that "Film" will become the central publication of the nationalist film movement, and start from all aspects of theoretical script creation, film criticism, and create a youthful situation in the Chinese film industry.

Finally, I hope that all colleagues in the Chinese film industry will quickly wake up and go to the road of the nationalist film movement, for our nation, for our films.

Manuscript Rules for Book and Newspaper Introductions 209

(1) The text is limited to the introduction of the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, education, etc. are listed in the introduction. However, boring books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) The pictures are limited to the latest works of new writers at home and abroad and the attached pictures related to the text.

(3) Texts such as textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(5) Each text should not exceed 3,000 words.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not write the manuscript horizontally, and do not write the characters in a cursive or sloppy manner. Western texts can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached under the translation.

(8) Do not draw pictures with blue ink, and do not use colored buttons. Black drawings must be made on white paper.

(9) Please indicate that the manuscript is received by the book and newspaper introduction editorial department.

(10) Manuscripts will not be returned regardless of whether they are published or not. If you need to return them, you should declare in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) (1) The remuneration for texts is divided into three types: 3 yuan, 2 yuan, and 1 yuan per thousand words. Pictures and photos are also the same for each. For example, there are special remunerated manuscripts

Youth Garden

Interesting Weekly Talks 210

— Bin

The Department of Journalism at Fudan University held its first meeting at Yiyuan

The Department of Journalism at Fudan University has been running for less than three semesters, but it has achieved remarkable results and has long been praised by people in the community. Even in comparison with other departments in the school, it can be regarded as a wonderful flower that has emerged later. The biggest reason for this is still the cooperation between teachers and students. Director Xie's guidance is effective. We can also say that the achievements of the Department of Journalism today are by no means accidental. Moreover, the colleagues in the department are full of talents. Important positions in the school, such as the Fudan News Agency and the Five-Day Journal, are all organized by these excellent colleagues. The cooperation between teachers and students is also stronger than other departments, because Director Xie and Professor Huang Tianpeng love students as much as their own siblings and children. Therefore, Professor Huang, who is in charge of the "Newspaper Organization" course, actively plans to organize a small-scale newspaper so that students can gain experience and knowledge of running a newspaper. At the same time, they can also take this opportunity to practice and prepare for future application in major domestic newspapers. It is really rare to see such enthusiastic teaching among professors in other schools.

We are now studying, especially those who are studying journalism, it is not enough to concentrate on burying our heads in books. Regarding these subjects, we must go outside to find more abundant knowledge. Of course, we must often come into contact with society. In short, it is very important to work hard for knowledge outside the textbook. Director Xie had already seen this, and in the shortest period of time, he organized a weekly talk, the time is uncertain, and students in the Department of Journalism can participate at will, as long as it does not conflict with the regular class. On the one hand, it can connect the feelings between teachers and students, and on the other hand, it can get a lot of common sense in casual talks, breaking the dull and boring life of the classroom. This is much more meaningful.

This first weekly talk was held at Yiyuan, under the new guidance of Director Xie. More than a dozen students walked to the destination together. Really, there is another kind of fun. After entering Yiyuan, the spirit is refreshed, because the air here is fresh. The dull and boring classroom life every day really makes people feel tired. Director Xie and others found a small pavilion and gathered together to talk, and the joy was indescribable. It is not something that my unflowering pen can describe vividly.

Director Xie announced the purpose of setting up a weekly talk course and the importance of guiding the correct life outside the classroom. Secondly, he also talked about the need for journalists to have flexible minds and keen characteristics. When interviewing for news, it is very difficult to find out the true age of a woman. But we journalists have to use our flexible minds at this time. Director Xie said that when I was studying in Japan, a class of students was sent out to practice interviewing, and they were asked to find out the true age of a young lady. However, this young lady refused to tell them no matter what. One of the students cleverly used his flexible mind. He first asked the young lady how many years she had graduated from a higher girls' school, and how old she was when she graduated. Then he talked about other women's issues, etc., and she answered them very faithfully with great interest. Soon after, the student asked her how many years it had been since she graduated, and she quickly said it without forgetting anything. At this time, the student had already reached the goal of interviewing the young lady's true age, because the young lady's age, as long as you add the number of years she graduated from high school to the number of years she has left the school, it is equal to the current age. At that time, the students who were sitting there were enlightened by Director Xie's words.

At this point, Ms. Guo Zhenyi, a talented student from the department, came. She transferred here from Ginling Women's University, so she has a good grasp of academic knowledge. But Director Xie laughed and said that the secret of finding out the true age of a woman is not told to women. Everyone was delighted. However, I have now written down this method and told it to most readers, not only to make up for Ms. Guo's lack of knowledge.

I will not describe the scenery of Yiyuan. I think readers all know it.
